Post-Prayer Adhkar and Supplications
Describes recommended post-prayer adhkar and du'a

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recite the recommended adhkar after fard salah in the correct order, as prescribed in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
After fard salah, sunnah is to recite Ayat al-Kursi, the three quls, tasbih/tahmid/takbir (33 each), then make du'a and wipe the face.

This passage from Nur al-Idah outlines the post-prayer adhkar that are considered sunnah in the Hanafi school. While the salah itself is complete, these adhkar complete the worship and bring barakah. Let's break down the sequence step by step.

Guided Path
1
Recite Ayat al-Kursi and the Mu'awwidhat
After the fard salah (before any sunnah prayers), recite Ayat al-Kursi (2:255) and the three quls: Surah al-Ikhlas, al-Falaq, an-Nas.
These are often recited together as a set.
2
Perform the Tasbihat
Glorify Allah (Subhan Allah) 33 times, praise Him (Alhamdulillah) 33 times, and magnify Him (Allahu Akbar) 33 times. Some narrations include a 34th 'La ilaha illallah' but the text combines them into tahlil next.
The order is tasbih, tahmid, takbir.
3
Recite the Tahlil
Then say: 'La ilaha illallah wahdahu la sharika lahu, lahul mulku wa lahul hamdu wa huwa 'ala kulli shay'in qadir.'
This completes the verbal adhkar.
4
Make Du'a with Raised Hands
Raise hands and supplicate for yourself and for all Muslims. There is no specific prescribed du'a; any good supplication suffices.
Du'a after fard salah is a time of acceptance.
5
Wipe the Face after Du'a
At the end of the du'a, wipe your face with both hands. This is considered sunnah in the Hanafi school based on prophetic practice.
Some scholars consider it mustahabb; the Hanafi view is that it is established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Then they supplicate for themselves and for the Muslims, raising their hands, and then they wipe their faces with them at the end.

Commentary
This passage provides the recommended (sunnah) adhkar and du'a after the obligatory salah. It instructs reciting Ayat al-Kursi, Surah al-Ikhlas, and the Mu'awwidhatayn, followed by tasbih (thirty-three times), tahmid (thirty-three times), and takbir (thirty-three times). Then the phrase of tahlil is said. Finally, the worshipper raises hands to make personal du'a for themselves and all Muslims, and concludes by wiping the face. This practice is considered mustahabb in the Hanafi school. The order follows the matn of Nur al-Idah.

Key Terms
آية الكرسي (Ayat al-Kursi): Verse 255 of Surah al-Baqarah, recited after prayer.
المعوذات (al-Mu'awwidhat): Here meaning al-Ikhlas and al-Mu'awwidhatayn (Surah al-Falaq and al-Nas).
مسح الوجه (mas'h al-wajh): Wiping the face with hands after completing du'a.

The Twelve Invalidators of Prayer (1–12)
First twelve of sixty-eight invalidators of salah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first twelve invalidators of salah and apply the Hanafi principle that forgetfulness does not excuse these invalidators.

Core Idea
Twelve actions nullify prayer, even if done forgetfully — speech, greeting, excessive movement, and eating are all invalidators.

The prayer is a sacred act with specific boundaries. The Hanafi school enumerates sixty-eight invalidators (mufsidat) that break the prayer. This lesson covers the first twelve, each of which nullifies the prayer whether done intentionally, mistakenly, or forgetfully. Understanding these boundaries protects the integrity of your salah.

Guided Path
1
Categorize by type
Group the twelve invalidators into categories: verbal actions (speech, supplication, greeting, returning greeting), physical actions (excessive movement, turning chest away from qiblah, shaking hands), and consumption (eating, drinking, clearing throat).
This helps memorization and shows the range of mufsidat.
2
Note the exception for forgetfulness
The text explicitly states that speaking even forgetfully invalidates the prayer. This is a key Hanafi rule: forgetfulness does not excuse these invalidators.
Contrast with some other schools that excuse forgetful speech.
3
Define 'excessive action'
The term 'al-'amal al-kathir' is left undefined quantitatively here. In Hanafi fiqh, it is typically considered as actions that would make an onlooker doubt you are in prayer, often defined as three successive movements.
This is a contextual judgment.
4
Define the chickpea rule for food between teeth
Eating food stuck between teeth only invalidates if the amount is significant, quantified as the size of a chickpea (qadr al-himmah). Lesser amounts are excused.
This threshold is specific to the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يُفسد الصلاة. وهو ثمانية وستون شيئاً: ١- الكلمة، ولو سهواً. ٢- أو خطأ. ٣- والدعاء بما يُشبه كلامنا. ٤- والسلام بنية التحية، ولو ساهياً. ٥- وردُّ السلام بلسانه. ٦- أو بالمصافحة. ٧- والعمل الكثير. ٨- وتحويل الصدر عن القبلة. ٩- وأكلُ شيءٍ من خارج فَمِه، ولو قَلَّ. ١٠- وأكلُ ما بين أسنانه إن كان كثيراً، وهو قَدْرُ الحمصة. ١١- وشربه. ١٢- والتنحنح بلا عُذر.
Chapter on what invalidates the prayer. And it is sixty-eight things: 1- Speech, even if forgetfully. 2- Or mistakenly. 3- Supplication resembling human speech. 4- Greeting with intention of salutation, even if forgetfully. 5- Returning the greeting by tongue. 6- Or by shaking hands. 7- Excessive action. 8- Turning the chest away from the qiblah. 9- Eating something from outside his mouth, even if little. 10- Eating what is between his teeth if it is a lot, which is the size of a chickpea. 11- Drinking. 12- Clearing the throat without excuse.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on invalidators of salah (mufsidat al-salah) in Nur al-Idah. The author states there are sixty-eight invalidators and lists the first twelve. These include: speaking (whether intended, forgetful, or mistaken), making a supplication that sounds like ordinary human speech, initiating salams, returning a greeting verbally or by handshake, excessive movement, turning the chest away from the qiblah, eating or drinking anything external, eating food stuck between teeth if it is a significant amount (size of a chickpea), and clearing the throat without a valid excuse. Each invalidator is clearly delineated for memorization. The Hanafi school holds that these nullify the prayer, some requiring a repeat (qada) and some making the prayer invalid.

Key Terms
الكلمة (al-kalimah): Any speech, even one word, invalidates the prayer.
العمل الكثير (al-'amal al-kathir): Excessive physical action in prayer that distracts from it.
قَدْرُ الحمصة (qadr al-himmah): Approximately the size of a chickpea; used to define excessive food between teeth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many things invalidate the prayer?
A) 12
B) 68
C) 33
D) 100

Key Takeaway
The first twelve invalidators of salah include speech, greeting, excessive movement, turning from qiblah, eating, drinking, and clearing throat without excuse — and forgetfulness does not excuse them.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

Speech, Greeting, and Excessive Action in Prayer
Lists the first eight nullifiers of prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the first eight invalidators of prayer and explain the Hanafi definition of excessive action.

Core Idea
Any word addressed to a human, even forgetfully, invalidates prayer; excessive action is that which leaves no doubt.

The first eight nullifiers form the foundation of understanding what breaks prayer. Speech, greeting, and movement are the most common pitfalls. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi standard for excessive action.

Guided Path
1
Identify each invalidator
Read items 1-8 from the list. Note each action and the ruling: all invalidate even if done forgetfully or mistakenly.
Memorize the sequence: word, mistake, supplication resembling speech, greeting with intention, returning greeting, shaking hands, excessive action, turning from qibla.
2
Define excessive action
The text provides the definition: any action that leaves an observer certain you are not in prayer. If ambiguous, it is little. The preferred view: three consecutive movements are many.
The word 'مختار' indicates the chosen view in the Hanafi school.
3
Distinguish little vs. excessive
Test scenarios: one small movement is little; three consecutive large moves are many. The observer test is key.
This differs from the Shafi'i school which defines by type (e.g., walking is always many).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما يُفسد الصلاة
وهو ثمانية وستون شيئاً:
باب
ما يُفسد الصلاة
١- الكلمة، ولو سهواً. ٢- أو خطأ.
٣- والدعاء بما يُشبه كلامنا.
٤- والسلام بنية التحية، ولو ساهياً. ٥- ورَدُّ السلام بلسانه. ٦- أو بالمصافحة.
٧- والعمل الكثير
(١) لا القليل والفاصل بينهما : أن الكثير هو الذي لا يشك الناظر لفاعله أنه ليس في الصلاة، وإن اشتبه فهو قليل، على الأصح، وهو قول العامة، وهو المختار، وقيل: الحركات الثلاث المتواليات كثير، ودونها : قليل. مراقي وطحطاوي.
٨- وتحويل الصدر عن القبلة.
٩ - وأكلُ شيءٍ من خارج فَمِه، ولو قَلَّ.
١٠ - وأكلُ ما بين أسنانه إن كان كثيراً، وهو قَدْرُ الحمصة.
١١ - وشربه.
١٢ ـ والتنحنح بلا عُذر.
(٢) أي لمخاطب حاضر. إعزاز ص ٢٣١
١٣- والتأفيف.
١٤ - والأنين.
١٥- والتأوه.
١٦ـ وارتفاع بكائه من وَجَع.
١٧ ـ أو مصيبة، لا من ذِكْرِ جَنَّةٍ، أو نار.
۱۸ - وتشميت عاطس بـ: «يَرحمك الله».
١٩ - وجواب مُستفهم عن ند الله بـ: «لا إله إلا الله».
٢٠ - وخَبَرِ سُوء: بالاسترجاع.
۲۱- وسار بـ: «الحمد لله».
۲۲ - وعَجَب بـ: «سبحان الله». ٢٣ - أو : «لا إله إلا الله».
٢٤ - وكُلُّ شيءٍ قصد به الجواب، كـ: ﴿يَيَحْيَى خُذِ الْكِتَابَ﴾ [مريم ١٢]، وذلك لمن طلب كتاباً.
٢٥- ورؤية متيمم ما (٢).
(٢) إن كان قبل قعوده قدر التشهد : تفسد باتفاق في المذهب، وإن كان بعد قعوده قدر التشهد : فتفسد عند الإمام، ولا تفسد عندهما وهي من المسائل الاثنا عشرية. طحطاوي ص ٢٦٥
٢٦- وتمام مدة ماسح الخف(٣).
(٣) أي وهو في الصلاة.
۲۷ - ونَزْعُه.
What invalidates the prayer. It is sixty-eight things: Chapter: What invalidates the prayer. 1- A word, even if forgetfully. 2- Or mistakenly. 3- And supplication that resembles our speech. 4- And greeting with the intention of greeting, even if forgetfully. 5- And returning the greeting with the tongue. 6- Or by shaking hands. 7- And excessive action. (1) Not little; the distinction between them: excessive is that which the observer of the doer does not doubt that he is not in prayer, and if it is ambiguous then it is little, according to the most correct view, and it is the statement of the general scholars, and it is the chosen view, and it is said: three consecutive movements are many, and less than that is little. (Maraqi wa Tahawi). 8- And turning the chest away from the qibla. 9- And eating something from outside his mouth, even if little. 10- And eating what is between his teeth if it is much, which is the size of a chickpea. 11- And drinking it. 12- And clearing the throat without excuse. (2) i.e., addressing a present addressee. (I'zaz, p. 231) 13- And saying 'uff'. 14- And groaning. 15- And sighing. 16- And his crying rising from pain. 17- Or from calamity, not from remembrance of paradise or hellfire. 18- And responding to a sneezer with 'Yarhamukallah'. 19- And answering someone who asks about Allah's religion with 'La ilaha illallah'. 20- And bad news with saying 'Inna lillahi wa inna ilayhi raji'un'. 21- And good news with 'Alhamdulillah'. 22- And wonder with 'Subhanallah'. 23- Or 'La ilaha illallah'. 24- And everything intended as a response, like (O Yahya, take the Scripture) [Maryam 12], that is for one who asks for a book. 25- And the seeing of water by the one who performs tayammum. (2) If it was before his sitting for the duration of tashahhud: it invalidates by agreement in the school, and if it was after his sitting for the duration of tashahhud: then it invalidates according to Imam [Abu Hanifa], and does not invalidate according to them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], and it is from the twelve issues. (Tahawi, p. 265) 26- And the completion of the period for the one wearing khuff. (3) i.e., while he is in prayer. 27- And removing them.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage is a list of nullifiers (mufsidat) of prayer from the Hanafi matn Nur al-Idah. The author states there are sixty-eight total, and this portion covers the first twenty-seven. Each item is a ruling: performing it intentionally or forgetfully invalidates the prayer unless an exception is noted. 

Key points from the footnotes: 
- Excessive action (al-‘amal al-kathir) is defined as movement that leaves no doubt to an observer that the person is not praying. If doubtful, it is considered little. The preferred view is that three consecutive movements are many; fewer are little. 
- Clearing the throat without an excuse invalidates; an excuse would be for recitation, but the footnote specifies it is 'addressing a present addressee', i.e., the throat-clearing is done to get someone's attention, which is like speech. 
- The dispute on item 25 (seeing water by a mutayammim) is a well-known intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. All agree that if the water is seen before sitting for tashahhud, the prayer is invalid. After sitting, Abu Hanifa holds it invalid, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it valid. This is one of the 'twelve issues' where they differ. 
- Item 26 (completion of the period for the one wiping over khuffs) means: if during prayer the valid wiping period ends, the prayer becomes invalid. Similarly, removing the khuffs during prayer invalidates it.

The list emphasizes that actions resembling human speech, intentional eating/drinking (even small amounts from outside the mouth), excessive movement, and turning away from qibla all nullify the prayer, along with other specific actions.

Key Terms
الكلمة (al-kalimah): Any word addressed to a human, even unintentionally, that invalidates prayer.
العمل الكثير (al-‘amal al-kathīr): Excessive action that leaves an observer certain the person is not in prayer; ambiguous actions are considered little.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling if a person in prayer turns their chest completely away from the qibla?
A) The prayer is invalid.
B) The prayer is valid but requires sajdah al-sahw.
C) The prayer is valid if done forgetfully.
D) The prayer is valid only if the person immediately returns.

Key Takeaway
The first eight nullifiers establish that speech, greeting, and excessive motion break the prayer, with the observer test defining excess.

Eating, Drinking, and Vocal Nullifiers in Prayer
Lists nullifiers 9–24 covering eating, drinking, and vocalizations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which eating/drinking actions invalidate prayer and explain the categories of vocal nullifiers.

Core Idea
Eating even a little from outside the mouth, drinking, and any vocal sound expressing worldly pain invalidate the prayer.

Items 9 to 24 cover a range of nullifiers involving eating, drinking, throat-clearing, and various vocal responses. The pattern is clear: any action that resembles human speech or expresses worldly matters breaks the prayer, while sounds of purely spiritual reflection are exempt.

Guided Path
1
Categorize eating and drinking rules
Items 9-11: Eating from outside the mouth (even a little) invalidates; eating food stuck between teeth invalidates if it is much (chickpea size); drinking invalidates.
The key distinction: outside vs. inside the mouth. If one swallows residual saliva with food particles, it's only invalid if the particle is large (chickpea size).
2
Identify vocal nullifiers
Items 12-17: Throat-clearing without excuse, saying 'uff', groaning, sighing, crying from pain or calamity. Crying from fear of paradise or hellfire is exempt.
The exemption for crying from spiritual reasons shows that not all sounds invalidate.
3
Recognize responses that invalidate
Items 18-24: Responding to a sneeze, answering a question about Allah's religion, saying 'inna lillah' for bad news, 'alhamdulillah' for good news, 'subhanallah' for wonder, and any verse quoted as a response.
The key principle: if the intention is to respond to someone, it invalidates.

Special Cases: Mutayammim Seeing Water and Khuff Rulings
Lists items 25-27 with a footnote on the mutayammim dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on a mutayammim seeing water during prayer and on the expiration/removal of khuff while in prayer.

Core Idea
The prayer of a mutayammim becomes invalid if water is seen before tashahhud; after tashahhud, the imams differ; completion of khuff period or removal during prayer invalidates.

The final three items address specific scenarios that combine purity and prayer. The mutayammim case involves a well-known intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, while the khuff rulings highlight how a change in purity status affects an ongoing prayer.

Guided Path
1
Understand the mutayammim scenario
Item 25: A person who cannot find water performs tayammum and begins prayer. During prayer, they see water. The ruling depends on timing: before sitting for tashahhud – all agree prayer invalidates; after sitting – Abu Hanifa says invalid, Sahibayn say valid.
The dispute is based on whether the obligation of tayammum has been fulfilled. After tashahhud, the prayer is nearly complete.
2
Apply the khuff rulings
Items 26-27: If the period for wiping over khuff expires during prayer, or if the person removes the khuff during prayer, the prayer becomes invalid. This is because the purification becomes nullified.
Removing khuff itself is an action that invalidates wudu? Actually, removing khuff does not break wudu, but it invalidates the prayer because the person is no longer in a state of purity for the prayer (since they were relying on the khuff wiping). The prayer was valid only with the khuff; once removed, the wudu is incomplete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

۲۷ - ونَزْعُه.
What invalidates the prayer. It is sixty-eight things: Chapter: What invalidates the prayer. 1- A word, even if forgetfully. 2- Or mistakenly. 3- And supplication that resembles our speech. 4- And greeting with the intention of greeting, even if forgetfully. 5- And returning the greeting with the tongue. 6- Or by shaking hands. 7- And excessive action. (1) Not little; the distinction between them: excessive is that which the observer of the doer does not doubt that he is not in prayer, and if it is ambiguous then it is little, according to the most correct view, and it is the statement of the general scholars, and it is the chosen view, and it is said: three consecutive movements are many, and less than that is little. (Maraqi wa Tahawi). 8- And turning the chest away from the qibla. 9- And eating something from outside his mouth, even if little. 10- And eating what is between his teeth if it is much, which is the size of a chickpea. 11- And drinking it. 12- And clearing the throat without excuse. (2) i.e., addressing a present addressee. (I'zaz, p. 231) 13- And saying 'uff'. 14- And groaning. 15- And sighing. 16- And his crying rising from pain. 17- Or from calamity, not from remembrance of paradise or hellfire. 18- And responding to a sneezer with 'Yarhamukallah'. 19- And answering someone who asks about Allah's religion with 'La ilaha illallah'. 20- And bad news with saying 'Inna lillahi wa inna ilayhi raji'un'. 21- And good news with 'Alhamdulillah'. 22- And wonder with 'Subhanallah'. 23- Or 'La ilaha illallah'. 24- And everything intended as a response, like (O Yahya, take the Scripture) [Maryam 12], that is for one who asks for a book. 25- And the seeing of water by the one who performs tayammum. (2) If it was before his sitting for the duration of tashahhud: it invalidates by agreement in the school, and if it was after his sitting for the duration of tashahhud: then it invalidates according to Imam [Abu Hanifa], and does not invalidate according to them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], and it is from the twelve issues. (Tahawi, p. 265) 26- And the completion of the period for the one wearing khuff. (3) i.e., while he is in prayer. 27- And removing them.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage is a list of nullifiers (mufsidat) of prayer from the Hanafi matn Nur al-Idah. The author states there are sixty-eight total, and this portion covers the first twenty-seven. Each item is a ruling: performing it intentionally or forgetfully invalidates the prayer unless an exception is noted. 

Key points from the footnotes: 
- Excessive action (al-‘amal al-kathir) is defined as movement that leaves no doubt to an observer that the person is not praying. If doubtful, it is considered little. The preferred view is that three consecutive movements are many; fewer are little. 
- Clearing the throat without an excuse invalidates; an excuse would be for recitation, but the footnote specifies it is 'addressing a present addressee', i.e., the throat-clearing is done to get someone's attention, which is like speech. 
- The dispute on item 25 (seeing water by a mutayammim) is a well-known intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. All agree that if the water is seen before sitting for tashahhud, the prayer is invalid. After sitting, Abu Hanifa holds it invalid, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it valid. This is one of the 'twelve issues' where they differ. 
- Item 26 (completion of the period for the one wiping over khuffs) means: if during prayer the valid wiping period ends, the prayer becomes invalid. Similarly, removing the khuffs during prayer invalidates it.

The list emphasizes that actions resembling human speech, intentional eating/drinking (even small amounts from outside the mouth), excessive movement, and turning away from qibla all nullify the prayer, along with other specific actions.

Key Terms
رؤية متيمم ما (ru’yat mutayammimin mā’): The act of a person performing tayammum seeing water during prayer, which may or may not invalidate the prayer depending on timing and which imam's view is followed.
تمام مدة ماسح الخف (tamām muddat māsih al-khuff): The completion of the permissible period for wiping over khuff (one day for resident, three for traveler) while still in prayer.
نزع الخف (naz‘ al-khuff): Removing the khuff during prayer; this invalidates the prayer because the purity based on wiping is lost.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is a point of consensus among the Hanafi imams regarding the mutayammim seeing water?
A) The prayer is invalid if water is seen after tashahhud.
B) The prayer is invalid if water is seen before tashahhud.
C) The prayer is valid regardless of when water is seen.
D) The prayer is valid only if the tayammum was for travel.

Key Takeaway
The mutayammim's prayer invalidates by consensus if water appears before tashahhud; after tashahhud, a valid ikhtilaf exists between Imam and Sahibayn.

Verbal Invalidators of Prayer (Items 13-24)
List of verbal invalidators of prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which verbal expressions and responses nullify the prayer according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Any speech intended as a response, even Quranic verses, invalidates the prayer.

The Hanafi school is meticulous about what constitutes permissible speech during prayer. This lesson covers the first category of invalidators: words or sounds that break the sanctity of salah. Understanding these helps preserve the validity of your worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the verbal acts
List the expressions mentioned: 'uff', groaning, moaning, crying from worldly pain or calamity, responding to a sneeze, answering a religious question, reacting to news, exclaiming at something amazing.
All of these are considered speech that is not part of the prayer.
2
Distinguish permissible from impermissible crying
Note the exception: crying from remembrance of Paradise or Hellfire does not invalidate, while crying from worldly causes does.
This is a key nuance.
3
Understand the principle of response
Any utterance intended as a reply, even a Quranic verse, invalidates because it is not dhikr for the prayer.
Example: saying 'O Yahya, take the Book' as a response is invalid.
4
Memorize the list
These are fundamental to avoid accidental nullification.
Use the numbered list as a mnemonic.

State-Change Invalidators of Prayer (Items 25-30, 36-37)
List of invalidators arising from changes in state or excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which changes in the worshipper's condition or circumstances nullify the prayer.

Core Idea
If the excuse for a concession vanishes, the prayer performed under that concession becomes invalid.

Certain people are allowed to pray with concessions: the one without water performs tayammum, the sick gestures, the one with a cast wipes over it. If their situation changes mid-prayer—finding water, healing—the prayer is no longer valid. Similarly, the end of an excuse (like bleeding) breaks the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the concession-based invalidators
The mutayammim sees water, the person wiping over khuffs finishes the period or removes them, the illiterate learns a verse, the naked finds clothing, the gesturer becomes able to bow and prostrate.
Each of these changes the person's legal ability to perform prayer with full conditions.
2
Note the timing of the change
The invalidator occurs at the moment the condition changes, not before or after. For example, if the mutayammim sees water before sitting for tashahhud, the prayer nullifies; if after, it is complete.
The text implies these changes invalidate only if they occur before the prayer is effectively concluded.
3
Include the removal of partial purity concessions
Items 36-37: the cast falling off after healing, and the excuse ending (e.g., bleeding stops). These are similar – the reason for the leniency disappears.
This connects to the chapter on wudu and prayer of the excused person.
4
Apply the principle
The underlying rule: if the condition that allowed a leniency (rukhsah) ceases, the prayer performed with that leniency becomes invalid because it was no longer valid after the change.
This is a key Hanafi legal maxim: 'When the excuse ceases, the ruling returns to the original.'

Temporal, Purity, and Mental Invalidators (Items 31-35, 38-43)
List of invalidators related to time, impurity, and mental state

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify invalidators related to time, ritual purity, and mental state.

Core Idea
Loss of sanity, ritual purity, or proper timing breaks the prayer instantly.

Some invalidators are beyond the worshipper's control: time expiring, falling unconscious, or becoming junub. Others are deliberate: intentional hadath. This lesson covers the remaining items that protect the integrity of salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the temporal invalidators
Items 31-35: remembering a missed prayer (for one with fixed order), appointing an unfit imam, sunrise during Fajr, sun passing zenith during Eid, entering Asr time during Jumu'ah.
These involve time-critical situations where the prayer's time window is violated.
2
Identify the purity and consciousness invalidators
Items 38-43: intentional hadath, hadath caused by someone else, unconsciousness, insanity, janaba from looking (without touch) or from wet dream.
Hadath (ritual impurity) and loss of mind nullify the prayer.
3
Understand the principle behind temporal invalidators
Each prayer has a defined time. If the prayer's time expires (e.g., sunrise during Fajr), the prayer becomes invalid because it is no longer within its valid period. Similarly, if a missed prayer with a fixed order is remembered, the current supererogatory prayer must be interrupted.
The fixed order (tartib) applies to prayers missed within a single day.
4
Note the nuance of hadath and janaba
Hadath invalidates whether intentional or accidental. Janaba from looking requires emission of fluid; looking alone without fluid does not cause janaba. Wet dream causes janaba unconsciously.
These are matters of ritual purity that break the state necessary for prayer.

Mufsidat al-Salat: Invalidators of Prayer
Enumeration of actions and events that invalidate prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the invalidators of prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain why each invalidates, distinguishing intentional from unintentional causes.

Core Idea
Prayer is invalidated by any event that breaks its continuity, whether intentional or not.

Preserving the validity of prayer is essential. The Hanafi school enumerates specific actions and events that nullify prayer. This lesson presents the comprehensive list from Nur al-Idah, a core matn, including conditions and exceptions. Understanding these invalidators helps you avoid them and know when repetition is required.

Guided Path
1
Categorize the invalidators
Group the listed invalidators into themes: changes in state, impurity, loss of senses, actions violating prayer sequence.
This helps memory and applied reasoning.
2
Identify the underlying cause
For each, determine why it invalidates: does it break continuity, violate a condition, or introduce impurity?
E.g., sunrise during Fajr breaks the prayer's time condition.
3
Note conditions and exceptions
Some invalidators have conditions (e.g., aligning with a woman) or exceptions (e.g., tasbih does not invalidate).
Refer to the footnotes in the text.
4
Apply to scenarios
Test your knowledge by reasoning through hypothetical situations.
E.g., what if someone recites Quran after hadath but before leaving? It invalidates.
5
Memorize systematically
Use the numbered list and thematic clusters for memorization.
Repetition and understanding aid retention.

What invalidates prayer
(1)
28 - The illiterate person learning a verse.
29 - The naked person finding a covering.
30 - The one gesturing being able to bow and prostrate. 31 - Remembering a missed prayer for one with order.
32 - Appointing as imam one who is not suitable as imam.
33 - Sunrise during Fajr. 34 - Its [sun] setting during 'Eid prayer.
(2)
35 - The entry of 'Asr time during Friday prayer(3).
36 - The plaster cast falling off after healing.
37 - The excuse of the excused person ceasing.
38 - Hadath (ritual impurity) intentionally.
39 - Or by the action of another.
40 - Unconsciousness.
41 - Insanity.
42 - Janabah (major impurity) by looking.
43 - Or by wet dream.
(1) And he was not following a reciter; because when he learns, he must recite with it.
(2) And it is during the prayer.
(3) Restricted to Friday prayer because Zuhr is not invalidated by the entry of 'Asr time.
44 - Aligning with a desired woman, in an absolute prayer, shared, with tahrimah, in a single place, without a barrier (3), and he did not gesture to her to step back, and he intended her as imam. 45 - The exposure of the 'awrah of one whom hadath preceded, even if forced to, like a woman uncovering her forearm for wudu. 46 - His recitation (4) while going or returning for wudu.
47 - His remaining the duration of performing a pillar after hadath preceded while awake.
48 - His passing by water close to him for another.
49 - His leaving the mosque due to suspicion of hadath.

50 - His passing through the rows outside of it due to suspicion. 51 - His leaving thinking he is not in wudu.
52 - Or that the period of his wiping has expired.
53 - Or that he has a missed prayer.
(1) Even if she is a mahram to him, or his wife. Maraqi.
(6)
(2) i.e., the actual prayer comprising tahrim and tahlil, ruku' and sujud; thus janazah prayer is not invalidated. Tahatawi. (3) The extent of a dhira' or a gap that accommodates a man, and he did not gesture to her to step back; if she does not step back by his gesture, her prayer is invalidated, not his. Maraqi.
(4) i.e., recitation of the Quran by one whom hadath preceded while going or returning, not his tasbih; thus it is not invalidated because it is not part of the prayer. Maraqi and Tahatawi.
(5) i.e., outside the mosque due to suspicion of hadath.
(6) i.e., suspicion of hadath and he did not actually commit hadath, like water coming from his nose. Maraqi.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a matn (text for memorization) enumerating the invalidators of prayer (mufsidat al-salat) according to the Hanafi school. The author lists 53 items, though many are grouped. We will follow the order of the text, explaining each invalidator briefly. The list begins with item 28: if an illiterate person (who cannot recite Quran) learns a verse during prayer, his prayer is invalidated because he must now recite that verse, which requires stopping the prayer's sequence. Item 29: if a naked person finds covering during prayer, his prayer is invalidated because he must cover himself, which involves action. Item 30: if one who was gesturing (due to inability) becomes able to bow and prostrate, the prayer is invalidated because he must perform the physical pillars. Item 31: remembering a missed prayer while performing a present prayer if there is a time-based order (tartib) invalidates the present prayer. Item 32: appointing an unsuitable person as imam invalidates the prayer. Items 33-34: sunrise during Fajr and sunset during 'Eid prayer invalidate those prayers. Items 35-37: entry of 'Asr time during Friday prayer, the plaster cast falling off after healing, and the excuse of the excused person ceasing invalidate the prayer. Items 38-43: intentional hadath (ritual impurity), hadath caused by another, unconsciousness, insanity, janabah by looking or wet dream all invalidate. Items 44-53 cover specific situations like aligning with a desirable woman, exposure of 'awrah, recitation after hadath, staying after hadath, passing by water, leaving the mosque on suspicion, etc. The text includes extensive footnotes clarifying conditions. The Hanafi position is that prayer becomes invalid when any of these occur, requiring repetition.

Key Terms
مُفْسِدَات الصلاة (mufsidaat al-salat): Actions or events that nullify the prayer, requiring its complete repetition.
الحدث (al-hadath): Ritual impurity that invalidates wudu, whether intentional or unintentional.
المشيئة (al-mashtah): A desired woman (literally 'one who is desired') – refers to a woman attractive to the man.

Key Takeaway
Prayer is invalidated by a specific set of actions and events; knowing them ensures that your worship is valid.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Nullifiers of Prayer (Mufsidat al-Salah)
Enumeration of actions that nullify the prayer, with focus on the one who has a hadath.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the actions that nullify the prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain the conditions under which each applies.

Core Idea
Nullifying the prayer requires specific actions, not just breaking wudu.

The prayer is a sacred obligation that, once started, must be carried to completion. However, certain events – from minor doubts to intentional acts – can nullify it entirely. This passage from Nur al-Idah systematically enumerates the nullifiers (mufsidat) that a Hanafi must know, with special attention to the one who experiences a hadath (break of wudu) during prayer. Understanding these rules protects the worshiper from invalidating their worship unknowingly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The passage first lists nullifiers that apply specifically to the one who has hadath (items 44-56), then general nullifiers (items 57-62). Note the common condition: most apply only if they occur before the final sitting of tashahhud.
Items 44-56 assume the person has already broken wudu; items 57-62 can apply to anyone.
2
Analyze conditions for each nullifier
For each item, note the exact conditions: e.g., for 'aligning with a desirable woman' (44), it must be at takbir, in a shared prayer, same place, no barrier, no gesture, and intent to lead. For 'prolonging hamzah in takbir' (57), the prolongation must change the meaning.
Some items have additional conditions from footnotes, like the difference between imam and follower.
3
Recognize intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Two key differences: (a) madd al-hamzah – Abu Hanifa says nullifies, Sahibayn say no; (b) nullifier after final sitting – the relied-upon view is that it does not nullify, but some say it does. Understand why each position is held.
These are legitimate differences of ijtihad; the mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view and the consensus on the final sitting.
4
Apply to a scenario
Take a concrete case: a person breaks wudu, then thinks he has impurity on his clothes, leaves the mosque, recites Quran on return, and continues. Identify each nullifier that occurred and state the overall ruling.
Items 49, 54, and 46 apply; prayer is invalid.

Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is from Nur al-Idah, a Hanafi matn on fiqh, listing the nullifiers (mufsidat) of the prayer. The author enumerates items 44 through 62, many of which concern the one who has preceded by an event (hadath) – i.e., who breaks wudu during prayer. Key points: Aligning with a desirable woman (item 44) at the opening takbir invalidates the prayer of both if done intentionally with intent to lead her? The footnotes clarify the conditions. Exposing the private part (item 45) even if forced (e.g., to wash for wudu) nullifies. Reciting Quran while going or returning for wudu (item 46) nullifies if one had an event; but not tasbih. Remaining silent for a full rukn (item 47) after an event also nullifies. Passing by water (item 48) and leaving the mosque due to suspicion (item 49) apply to the one who had an event. Items 50-53 continue: passing rows outside mosque, departing thinking no wudu, thinking wipe duration expired, thinking he has a missed prayer. Item 54: impurity thinking. Item 55: prompting a non-imam. Item 56: takbir intending to switch prayers. The general condition: these nullify only if they occur before the final sitting equal to tashahhud (footnote explains ikhtilaf after that). Items 57-62 add: prolonging the hamzah in the takbir (footnote: Abu Hanifa says invalidates; the two companions say no), reciting from Quran if not memorized, performing a rukn or having time for it while naked or with impurity, the follower preceding the imam in a pillar, and a masbuq following the imam in sajdat al-sahw after he separated. The footnotes are from Sharh al-Maraqi and al-Tahtawi. All these are mufsidat in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
المشتهاة (al-mushtahāh): A desirable woman whom one may lawfully enjoy (wife or slave), or even a mahram according to some.
سبق الحدث (sabaqahu al-ḥadath): One who is overtaken by an event (breaking wudu) during prayer.
مَدُّ الهمزة (madd al-hamzah): Prolonging the hamzah in the takbir (e.g., in 'Allahu Akbar') so that it becomes prolonged to the point of changing the meaning.
المفسدات (al-mufsidāt): Actions or events that invalidate the prayer when they occur with their conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Remaining silent for the duration of a rukn
B) Reciting tasbih while going for wudu
C) Walking to a nearby water source without leaving the mosque
D) Prompting the imam

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school enumerates specific nullifiers, many applying to the one who suffers a hadath; understanding each condition is essential to preserve the validity of one's prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Invalidators of Prayer (Mufsidat al-Salah)
Lists invalidators of salah with Hanafi conditions and intra-madhhab disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the invalidators of prayer according to the Hanafi school, distinguish between agreed-upon and disputed items, and apply the critical condition of the final sitting to determine validity.

Core Idea
Prayer is invalidated by specific actions; the timing relative to the final sitting determines the ruling.

The Hanafi school enumerates a detailed list of actions that nullify the prayer. Understanding these invalidators (mufsidat) is crucial for every Muslim to preserve the validity of their salah. This lesson unpacks the list from Nur al-Idah, highlighting key conditions and internal scholarly differences.

Guided Path
1
Understand the timing condition
Many invalidators only nullify the prayer if they occur before the final sitting of tashahhud. After that, the prayer is considered complete and not invalidated by those actions.
This is a critical nuance: exiting the prayer after the final sitting is wajib, not fard, so the prayer remains valid.
2
Categorize the invalidators
Group the invalidators by type: speech-related (takbir with wrong intention, reading from mushaf, incorrect salam), action-related (preceding the imam, exposing 'awrah, performing a rukn with impurity), and impurity/cleanliness (remaining in hadath, carrying preventing impurity).
This categorization aids memorization and application.
3
Note the intra-madhhab disputes
Two items are disputed between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): prolonging the hamza in the takbir (no. 57) and intentional hadath after the final sitting (no. 66). The preferred view follows the companions.
The mufta bihi for both is non-invalidation.
4
Apply the rulings to the masbuq scenario
The masbuq (latecomer) has unique invalidators, such as following the imam in sujud al-sahw after separation (no. 62) and the imam's laughter affecting only the masbuq (no. 65). Understand the reasoning: the invalidator occurs in the middle of the masbuq's prayer.
This shows how the same action affects the imam and masbuq differently.

(Imdad al-Fattah; see Ṭahtawi p. 226) (3) And according to the two companions, it does not invalidate. (Ṭahtawi) (4) That is, the passage of time sufficient for performing a rukn. (Marqi) (5) For example, if he bowed and raised his head before the imam and did not repeat it with him or after him. (6) That is, the masbuq stood after the imam's salam and bound his rak‘ah with a sajdah, then the imam remembered sujud al-sahw, and the masbuq followed him: his prayer is invalidated because he followed him after the occurrence of separation and its obligation. (Marqi) 63. And not repeating the final sitting after performing an essential sajdah that he remembered after sitting. (1) 64. And not repeating a rukn performed while sleeping. 65. (I‘zaz) (3) The amount of tashahhud according to the Imam, and the two companions said: it does not invalidate. (Ṭahtawi) (4) Meaning intentionally. (5) Because it is intentional salam with the intention of cutting off before its time, so the prayer is invalidated. (Marqi)
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement enumerating the invalidators of prayer (mufsidat al-salah) according to the Hanafi school. The list begins with items numbered 54-68, continuing from an earlier section. Numbers 54-56: invalidators include remaining in impurity without leaving the mosque, correcting the imam incorrectly (for a non-imam), and pronouncing the takbir intending to transition to another prayer. These only invalidate if they occur before the final sitting of the tashahhud. Footnote (1) explains that if the contradictory action happens just before salam after the final sitting, the prayer is valid according to the preferred view, as exiting prayer by one's own action is obligatory (wajib), not fard. Number 57: prolonging the hamza in the takbir (especially in Allahu Akbar) invalidates the prayer. Footnote (2) specifies this is about the takbir of tahrimah; the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it does not invalidate (Footnote 3). Number 58: reading from a mushaf (book) what one does not memorize invalidates because it resembles action outside prayer. Number 59-60: performing a rukn or having the ability to do so while the ‘awrah is uncovered or with a preventing impurity invalidates. Number 61: the muqtadi preceding the imam in a rukn and not repeating it invalidates. Number 62: a masbuq following the imam in sujud al-sahw invalidates because the masbuq had already separated. Numbers 63-64: not repeating the final sitting after remembering an essential sajdah, or not repeating a rukn performed while asleep, invalidates because the pillar was not properly performed. Number 65: the laughter (qahqaha) of the imam of a masbuq invalidates only the masbuq's prayer, as the invalidator occurs in the middle of his prayer. Number 66: intentional hadath (ritual impurity) after the final sitting of the tashahhud—according to Abu Hanifa it invalidates, but the two companions say it does not. Number 67-68: saying salam after two rak‘ahs in a non-two-rak‘ah prayer intentionally, due to mistaken assumption (traveler, Friday, etc.) or due to being a new Muslim, invalidates because it is an intentional premature termination.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): One who joins the prayer late and misses one or more rak'ahs with the imam.
قهقهة (qahqaha): Loud laughter that disrupts the prayer; specifically, laughter with sound and two letters like 'ha'.
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity that nullifies wudu, such as passing wind or urine.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a masbuq follows the imam in sujud al-sahw after the imam has already given salam and the masbuq has stood up to complete his prayer?
A) The masbuq's prayer is valid because sujud al-sahw is obligatory for all.
B) The masbuq's prayer is invalidated because he re-joined the imam after separation.
C) The masbuq's prayer is valid, and he should perform sujud al-sahw on his own.
D) The imam's prayer is invalidated due to the masbuq's action.

Key Takeaway
Prayer is invalidated by a specific set of actions; the timing relative to the final sitting and the existence of intra-madhhab disputes require careful application.

Invalidators of Prayer: Cases 63-68
Listing of six invalidators of prayer with footnotes explaining key details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six invalidators of prayer (cases 63-68) and explain the rulings for each, including the intra-Hanafi difference on deliberate speech after the final sitting.

Core Idea
Knowing when a seemingly minor action invalidates prayer protects one from unintentional nullification.

The prayer is a precise act of worship with clear boundaries. Even small errors—like forgetting a prostration or laughing at the wrong moment—can invalidate it if not handled correctly. This lesson examines six specific invalidators from the matn of Nur al-Idah, including a key difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions on speech after the final sitting.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish omission vs. commission
Note that some invalidators are failures to repeat (cases 63-64) while others are positive actions (65-68).
Both types break the continuity of prayer.
2
Identify the common thread
Each invalidator disrupts the proper sequence or intention of prayer. For example, forgetting a prostration breaks the sequence; laughing breaks the dignity.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Case 66 (deliberate speech after final sitting) has disagreement: Abu Hanifa says it invalidates; Sahibayn say it does not. Understand the reasoning behind each.
The mufta bihi is the cautious view of Abu Hanifa in later works.
4
Apply to the latecomer (masbuq)
Case 65 shows that the imam's laughter invalidates only the masbuq's prayer because it occurs in the middle of the masbuq's prayer, even if the imam has finished.
This illustrates that prayer is considered individually for the masbuq after the imam's final sitting.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement listing additional invalidators of prayer (mufsidat) from the matn of Nur al-Idah, with explanatory footnotes. The author presents six cases (63-68) where the prayer becomes invalid. Key points: (63) If one remembers a missed prostration after the final sitting, he must perform it and repeat the sitting; failure to do so invalidates. (64) Performing a pillar while sleeping does not require repetition; omission is excused. (65) Laughter by the imam after the latecomer has joined invalidates only the latecomer's prayer, as it occurs in the middle of his prayer. (66) Deliberate speech after the final sitting is invalid; the measure is the amount of tashahhud according to Abu Hanifa, but the two companions (Sahibayn) hold it does not invalidate. (67-68) Deliberately ending prayer after two rak'ahs in a non-two-rak'ah prayer, whether due to mistaken belief of travel, Friday, Tarawih, or recent conversion, invalidates the prayer. The footnotes provide proofs and references to other sources like Maraqi al-Falah and Tahatawi.

Key Terms
سجدة صُلْبيَّة (sajdah sulbiyyah): A prostration that is part of the spinal vertebra, meaning a prostration that is owed as a pillar of prayer.
قَهْقَهَة (qahqahah): Laughter that is audible, as opposed to just smiling.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A latecomer who joins the prayer after the imam has already started, thus missing some rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Six specific actions or omissions can invalidate prayer, including failure to correct a remembered prostration, omission of a repeated pillar, laughter of the imam affecting the latecomer, deliberate speech after final sitting (per Abu Hanifa), mistaken early salam, and a new Muslim's misunderstanding of rak'ah count.

Four Actions That Do Not Invalidate the Prayer
Listing actions that do not break the prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four actions listed in the Hanafi school that do not invalidate the prayer and identify the conditions that keep them from nullifying.

Core Idea
Minor, unintrusive actions do not break prayer; knowing them prevents unnecessary repetition.

The Hanafi school recognizes that not every incidental action during prayer invalidates it. This brief passage from Nur al-Idah lists four specific cases where the prayer remains valid, even if the action is blameworthy in some cases. Understanding these exceptions helps the believer maintain focus without undue scrupulosity.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Begin by noting that the passage opens a chapter on what does not invalidate (yufsid) the prayer. The default is that prayer is broken by deliberate acts, but here exceptions are given.
2
List the four actions
Identify each action: looking at a written text and understanding it; eating food particles between teeth less than a chickpea in size without excessive movement; a passerby moving in front of the worshiper within the place of prostration; looking at the internal private part of a revocably divorced woman with desire.
Each action has specific conditions that must be met for the prayer to remain valid.
3
Analyze the conditions for each
For eating: the morsel must be less than a chickpea (حمصة) and there must be no 'much action' (عمل كثير). For looking at the divorced woman: she must be in the revocable divorce period (رجعة) and the looking is with desire. For the passerby: the prayer remains valid even though the passerby commits a sin.
The condition of 'much action' is key: many small movements can accumulate to invalidate.
4
Connect to related rulings in footnotes
The footnote explains that the divorced woman is the revocably divorced (الرجعية), and the same ruling applies to looking at a non-mahram woman. It also notes that such looking establishes the prohibition of affinity (حرمة المصاهرة) with her female relatives, but the prayer is not invalidated.
This shows that some actions may have legal consequences even while not breaking the prayer.
5
Summarize the overarching principle
Conclude that any action that is minor, unintentional, or not considered 'much action' does not invalidate. The school balances the sacredness of prayer with human fallibility.
These rulings are from Zahir al-Riwayah and are mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Source Text

(1) أي فرجها الداخل.

Chapter: What does not invalidate the prayer. 1- If the praying person looks at a written text and understands it. 2- Or eats what is between his teeth, and it is less than a chickpea, without much action. 3- Or a passerby passes in his place of prostration: it does not invalidate, although the passerby sins. 4- And it is not invalidated by his looking at the private part (1) of the divorced woman (2) with desire, according to the chosen opinion, even if the return is established by it. ***** (1) i.e., her internal private part. (2) i.e., the revocably divorced woman, as evidenced by his saying shortly: 'even if the return is established by it.' Similarly, the ruling regarding his looking at a foreign woman, and the prohibition of affinity is established, so her mother and grandmothers become forbidden absolutely from her father's and mother's side however high, but her daughter is not forbidden except by consummation. Refer to Muraqi and Tahatawi, with addition from Ibn Abidin 3/30, al-Babi edition.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a chapter listing four actions that do not invalidate the prayer according to the Hanafi school. First, looking at a written text and understanding its meaning does not break the prayer. Second, eating food particles between teeth smaller than a chickpea without excessive movement is allowed. Third, if someone passes in front of the praying person within the place of prostration, the prayer remains valid although the passerby commits a sin. Fourth, looking at the private parts of a revocably divorced woman with desire does not invalidate the prayer, even if it establishes the right of return (رجعة). The footnote clarifies that 'divorced woman' refers to the revocably divorced (الرجعية), and similar ruling applies to looking at a non-mahram woman: it does not invalidate prayer but establishes prohibition of affinity (حرمة المصاهرة) with her female relatives.

Key Terms
مطلقة (mutallaqah): A divorced woman; in this context, specifically the revocably divorced woman (الرجعية) as per the footnote.
فرج (farj): Private part; here specifically the internal private part.
حمصة (himmasa): A chickpea; used as a measure for the size of food that does not invalidate.
رجعة (ruj'ah): Return; the right of the husband to take back his wife during the waiting period of a revocable divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Four specific actions (looking at text, eating small remnants, someone passing, looking at a revocably divorced woman's private part) do not invalidate the Hanafi prayer, provided their conditions are met.

The Categories of Makruh in Prayer: Tanzihi vs Tahrimi
List of disliked acts in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between makruh tanzihi and makruh tahrimi and apply the Hanafi classification to the first nine disliked acts in prayer.

Core Idea
Leaving a sunnah is lightly disliked, but its severity depends on the emphasis of the sunnah.

This passage from Nur al-Idah begins listing seventy-seven disliked acts in prayer. The Hanafi school distinguishes between two levels of dislike: tanzihi (light) and tahrimi (prohibitive). Understanding this distinction is crucial for properly weighting acts in prayer. The footnote from Ibn Abidin clarifies that leaving a sunnah is always at least makruh tanzihi, but the degree varies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
For each act listed, determine if it involves leaving a wajib or sunnah, or a physical action like cracking fingers or turning the neck.
The first item is 'leaving a wajib' – this is more severe than leaving a sunnah.
2
Classify the degree of dislike
Using Ibn Abidin's note, classify each act as tanzihi or tahrimi. Leaving a sunnah is tanzihi but can approach tahrimi if the sunnah is strongly emphasized.
The footnote states that the degree of tanzihi varies with the emphasis of the sunnah.
3
Apply the memorization anchor
Recognize that this list serves as a memorization anchor for common makruh acts. Commit the first nine to memory as a foundation for the broader list.
The full list has 77 items; mastering these nine aids recall of the rest.

(٢) قال ابن عابدين ١٣٣/٤ : «ترك السنة : مكروه تنزيهاً، ومرجعه: إلى ما تركه أولى، وتتفاوت التنزيهية في الشدة والقرب من التحريمية بحسب تأكد السنة، فإن مراتب الاستحباب متفاوتة كمراتب السنة والواجب والفرض فكذا أضدادها، كما أفاد في شرح المنية». اهـ، وينظر أيضاً ابن عابدين ١٨٦/٤ .
Chapter: Disliked matters in prayer. The praying person dislikes (i.e., it is disliked for him) seventy-seven things: 1- Leaving an obligatory act. 2- Leaving a sunnah, intentionally, playing with his clothing and body. 3- Turning pebbles, except for prostration once. 4- Cracking fingers. 5- Interlocking fingers. 6- Putting hands on hips. 7- Turning the neck. 8- Sitting on heels (iqa'). 9- Spreading forearms. (1) Includes what follows: disliked, either tanzihan (lightly) or tahriman (prohibitively). (2) Ibn Abidin said: 'Leaving the sunnah is lightly disliked, and its reference is that leaving it is better, and the degree of lightness varies in severity and nearness to prohibition according to the emphasis of the sunnah, because the ranks of recommendation vary like the ranks of sunnah, wajib, and fard, and similarly their opposites, as mentioned in Sharh al-Munyah.' End. See also Ibn Abidin 4/186.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on disliked acts (makruhat) in prayer, listing the first nine of seventy-seven items. The Hanafi school distinguishes between makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked) and makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). The list includes leaving a wajib (obligatory act) and leaving a sunnah intentionally, as well as physical actions like playing with clothing, turning pebbles unnecessarily, cracking or interlocking fingers, placing hands on hips, turning the neck, sitting on one's heels (iqa'), and spreading forearms on the ground. The footnote from Ibn Abidin clarifies that leaving a sunnah is makruh tanzihi, but the degree of dislike depends on how emphasized the sunnah is; more emphasized sunnah have closer to prohibitive dislike. This nuance is important because students often treat all makruh equally, but Hanafi fiqh recognizes a spectrum.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; an act that is discouraged but not forbidden. Includes both tanzihi (lightly) and tahrimi (prohibitively) disliked.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act; leaving it is makruh tanzihi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked)
C) Haram (forbidden)
D) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between light and prohibitive dislike (makruh tanzihi and tahrimi) in prayer, with the degree of dislike for leaving a sunnah depending on its emphasis.

The First Twenty-Five Disliked Acts in Prayer
Listing of disliked acts in prayer from Nur al-Idah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first twenty-five disliked acts (makruhat) in prayer according to the Hanafi school and distinguish between makruh tanzihi and makruh tahrimi.

Core Idea
Seventy-seven actions are disliked in prayer; the first twenty-five include omitting wajib/sunnah, playing with body/garment, and specific postures.

The Hanafi school places great emphasis on the adab (etiquette) of prayer. Beyond the obligatory and recommended acts, there are actions that are disliked (makruh). In this section from Nur al-Idah, we learn the first twenty-five of seventy-seven such actions. Understanding these helps preserve khushu' (concentration) and avoid compromising one's prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling category
Note that 'makruh' here encompasses both makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked, not sinful) and makruh tahrimi (close to haram). The footnote from Ibn Abidin clarifies that omitting a sunnah is makruh tanzihan, and the intensity varies.
2
Group the items by type
Categorize each item: omissions (wajib, sunnah), physical fidgeting (cracking fingers, interlacing, playing with body/clothing), postures (iq'a', spreading forearms, tashmir), clothing issues (praying in trousers, sadl, i'tijar), and recitation faults (lengthening, repeating surah, skipping order).
This grouping aids memorization.
3
Note the exceptions
Item 3 specifies 'except for prostration, once' – turning pebbles once for a valid reason is not disliked. Similarly, some items have conditions (e.g., rolling up sleeves before prayer if done before entering prayer leads to ikhtilaf).
4
Apply the underlying principle
The common illa (cause) for most items is that they distract from khushu' or display casualness. Actions that compromise humility or proper posture are generally disliked.
This principle helps extend to similar actions not listed.
5
Memorize the list
Use the categories as a mnemonic. Practice reciting the list in order. The numbers 1-25 correspond to the first 25 items in the matn.

(1) يشمل ما يلي المكروه تنزيهاً وتحريماً.
(٢) قال ابن عابدين ١٣٣/٤ : «ترك السنة : مكروه تنزيهاً، ومرجعه: إلى ما تركه أولى، وتتفاوت التنزيهية في الشدة والقرب من التحريمية بحسب تأكد السنة، فإن مراتب الاستحباب متفاوتة كمراتب السنة والواجب والفرض فكذا أضدادها، كما أفاد في شرح المنية». اهـ، وينظر أيضاً ابن عابدين ١٨٦/٤ .

ضرورة. مراقي.
On the disliked acts of prayer. (1) Section: On the disliked acts of prayer. It is disliked for the one praying seventy-seven things: 1 - Omitting an obligatory act. 2 - (Omitting) a sunnah, intentionally, or playing with his garment or body. - Turning over pebbles, except for prostration, once. 4 - Cracking the fingers. 5 - Interlacing them. 6 - Placing hands on hips. 7 - Turning the neck. 8 - Squatting (iq'a'). 9 - Spreading the forearms. (1) It includes what follows from disliked acts of tanzih and tahrim. (2) Ibn Abidin said: 'Omitting a sunnah is makruh tanzihan, and its meaning: leaving it is better, and the tanzih varies in intensity and closeness to tahrim according to the strength of the sunnah, for the levels of recommendation vary like the levels of sunnah, wajib, and fard, and similarly their opposites, as stated in Sharh al-Munya.' End. And also see Ibn Abidin 4/186. 10 - Rolling up his sleeves from them (i.e., his forearms). On the disliked acts of prayer. 11 - Praying in trousers while able to wear a shirt. 12 - Responding to the greeting (salam) with a gesture. 13 - Sitting cross-legged without an excuse. 14 - Braiding his hair. 15 - Al-i'tijar: wrapping the head in a cloth leaving the middle uncovered. 16 - Folding the garment. 17 - Letting it hang loose (sadl). 18 - Wrapping himself in it without taking out his hands. 19 - Placing the garment under his right armpit and throwing both sides over his left shoulder. (2). 20 - Reciting in other than the standing posture. 21 - Lengthening the first rak'ah in supererogatory prayer. 22 - Lengthening the second over the first in all prayers. 23 - Repeating a surah in one rak'ah of obligatory prayer. 24 - Reciting a surah above that which he recited (i.e., skipping ahead in order). 25 - Separating with a surah between two surahs he recited in two rak'ahs. (1) i.e., from his forearms, whether to the elbows or not according to the apparent view, and if he rolled them up before the prayer and then entered it: there is disagreement on the dislike (Tahawi). (2) Or the opposite; because covering the shoulders is recommended in prayer, so leaving it is disliked tanzihan without necessity. (Maraqi).
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a section from the matn of Nur al-Idah listing disliked acts (makruhat) in prayer. The author states that there are seventy-seven such acts, but in this portion we have the first twenty-five. The first footnote clarifies that 'makruh' here includes both makruh tanzihi (reprehensible but not sinful) and makruh tahrimi (close to prohibited). The second footnote quotes Ibn Abidin explaining that omitting a sunnah is makruh tanzihan, meaning it is better not to omit it, and the degree of dislike varies with the strength of the sunnah. The list begins with omitting a wajib (obligatory element) and a sunnah intentionally, or playing with one's garment or body. Then follow specific actions: turning over pebbles (except once for prostration), cracking fingers, interlacing them, placing hands on hips, turning the neck, squatting (iq'a'), spreading forearms, rolling up sleeves, praying in trousers while able to wear a shirt, responding to salam with a gesture, sitting cross-legged without excuse, braiding hair, al-i'tijar (wrapping head leaving middle bare), folding the garment, letting it hang loose (sadl), wrapping oneself without taking out hands, putting garment under right armpit and throwing sides over left shoulder, reciting in other than standing, lengthening the first rak'ah in nafl, lengthening the second rak'ah over the first in all prayers, repeating a surah in one rak'ah of fard, reciting a surah above the one recited (jumping order), and separating with a surah between two surahs recited in two rak'ahs. Each of these is considered makruh according to the Hanafi school, with some being tanzihi and others tahrimi depending on the strength of the evidence. The student should memorize these as they form an important part of adab al-salat.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): In this passage, 'makruh' refers to actions that are disliked in prayer, covering both makruh tanzihi (less severe) and makruh tahrimi (more severe).
تنزيهاً (tanzihan): A disliked act that is not sinful but better avoided; the omission of a recommended act without necessity.
تحريماً (tahriman): A disliked act that is close to prohibited; if done, it is sinful though not as severe as haram.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act of the Prophet; its omission without excuse is disliked (makruh tanzihan).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn, what is the ruling on a person who prays while rolling up his sleeves before entering prayer?
A) It is permissible without dislike.
B) It is makruh (disliked).
C) It invalidates the prayer.
D) It is sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Knowing the first twenty-five makruhat helps preserve khushu' in prayer and avoid actions that reduce reward; they range from tanzihi to tahrimi based on severity.
